This helps performance on both the client and the server. This configuration controls the \"\n                                                 + \"default batch size in bytes. \"\n                                                 + \"<p>\"\n                                                 + \"No attempt will be made to batch records larger than this size. \"\n                                                 + \"<p>\"\n                                                 + \"Requests sent to brokers will contain multiple batches, one for each partition with data available to be sent. \"\n                                                 + \"<p>\"\n                                                 + \"A small batch size will make batching less common and may reduce throughput (a batch size of zero will disable \"\n                                                 + \"batching entirely). A very large batch size may use memory a bit more wastefully as we will always allocate a \"\n                                                 + \"buffer of the specified batch size in anticipation of additional records.\"\n                                                 + \"<p>\"\n                                                 + \"Note: This setting gives the upper bound of the batch size to be sent. If we have fewer than this many bytes accumulated \"\n                                                 + \"for this partition, we will 'linger' for the <code>linger.ms</code> time waiting for more records to show up. \"\n                                                 + \"This <code>linger.ms</code> setting defaults to 5, which means the producer will wait for 5ms or until the record batch is \"\n                                                 + \"of <code>batch.size</code> (whichever happens first) before sending the record batch. Note that broker backpressure can \"\n                                                 + \" result in a higher effective linger time than this setting. \"\n                                                 + \"The default changed from 0 to 5 in Apache Kafka 4.0 as the efficiency gains from larger batches typically result in \"\n                                                 + \"similar or lower producer latency despite the increased linger.\";\n\n    /** <code>partitioner.adaptive.partitioning.enable</code> */\n    public static final String PARTITIONER_ADPATIVE_PARTITIONING_ENABLE_CONFIG = \"partitioner.adaptive.partitioning.enable\";\n    private static final String PARTITIONER_ADPATIVE_PARTITIONING_ENABLE_DOC =\n            \"When set to 'true', the producer will try to adapt to broker performance and produce more messages to partitions hosted on faster brokers. \"\n            + \"If 'false', the producer will try to distribute messages uniformly. This controls the \"\n                                           + \" durability of records that are sent. The following settings are allowed: \"\n                                           + \" <ul>\"\n                                           + \" <li><code>acks=0</code> If set to zero then the producer will not wait for any acknowledgment from the\"\n                                           + \" server at all. The record will be immediately added to the socket buffer and considered sent. No guarantee can be\"\n                                           + \" made that the server has received the record in this case, and the <code>retries</code> configuration will not\"\n                                           + \" take effect (as the client won't generally know of any failures). The offset given back for each record will\"\n                                           + \" always be set to <code>-1</code>.\"\n                                           + \" <li><code>acks=1</code> This will mean the leader will write the record to its local log but will respond\"\n                                           + \" without awaiting full acknowledgement from all followers. In this case should the leader fail immediately after\"\n                                           + \" acknowledging the record but before the followers have replicated it then the record will be lost.\"\n                                           + \" <li><code>acks=all</code> This means the leader will wait for the full set of in-sync replicas to\"\n                                           + \" acknowledge the record. This guarantees that the record will not be lost as long as at least one in-sync replica\"\n                                           + \" remains alive. This is the strongest available guarantee. This is equivalent to the acks=-1 setting.\"\n                                           + \"</ul>\"\n                                           + \"<p>\"\n                                           + \"Note that enabling idempotence requires this config value to be 'all'.\"\n                                           + \" If conflicting configurations are set and idempotence is not explicitly enabled, idempotence is disabled.\";\n\n    /** <code>linger.ms</code> */\n    public static final String LINGER_MS_CONFIG = \"linger.ms\";\n    private static final String LINGER_MS_DOC = \"The producer groups together any records that arrive in between request transmissions into a single batched request. \"\n                                                + \"Normally this occurs only under load when records arrive faster than they can be sent out. However in some circumstances the client may want to \"\n                                                + \"reduce the number of requests even under moderate load. This setting accomplishes this by adding a small amount \"\n                                                + \"of artificial delay&mdash;that is, rather than immediately sending out a record, the producer will wait for up to \"\n                                                + \"the given delay to allow other records to be sent so that the sends can be batched together. This can be thought \"\n                                                + \"of as analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. This setting gives the upper bound on the delay for batching: once \"\n                                                + \"we get <code>\" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \"</code> worth of records for a partition it will be sent immediately regardless of this \"\n                                                + \"setting, however if we have fewer than this many bytes accumulated for this partition we will 'linger' for the \"\n                                                + \"specified time waiting for more records to show up. This setting defaults to 5 (i.e. 5ms delay). Increasing <code>\" + LINGER_MS_CONFIG + \"=50</code>, \"\n                                                + \"for example, would have the effect of reducing the number of requests sent but would add up to 50ms of latency to records sent in the absence of load.\"\n                                                + \"The default changed from 0 to 5 in Apache Kafka 4.0 as the efficiency gains from larger batches typically result in \"\n                                                + \"similar or lower producer latency despite the increased linger.\";\n\n    /** <code>request.timeout.ms</code> */\n    public static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG;\n    private static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC\n        + \" This should be larger than <code>replica.lag.time.max.ms</code> (a broker configuration)\"\n        + \" to reduce the possibility of message duplication due to unnecessary producer retries.\";\n\n    /** <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> */\n    public static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = \"delivery.timeout.ms\";\n    private static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = \"An upper bound on the time to report success or failure \"\n            + \"after a call to <code>send()</code> returns. Available options are:\" +\n            \"<ul>\" +\n            \"<li>If not set, the default partitioning logic is used. \" +\n            \"This strategy send records to a partition until at least \" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \" bytes is produced to the partition. It works with the strategy:\" +\n            \"<ol>\" +\n            \"<li>If no partition is specified but a key is present, choose a partition based on a hash of the key.</li>\" +\n            \"<li>If no partition or key is present, choose the sticky partition that changes when at least \" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \" bytes are produced to the partition.</li>\" +\n            \"</ol>\" +\n            \"</li>\" +\n            \"<li><code>org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.RoundRobinPartitioner</code>: A partitioning strategy where \" +\n            \"each record in a series of consecutive records is sent to a different partition, regardless of whether the 'key' is provided or not, \" +\n            \"until partitions run out and the process starts over again. Note: There's a known issue that will cause uneven distribution when a new batch is created. \" +\n            \"See KAFKA-9965 for more detail.\" +\n            \"</li>\" +\n            \"</ul>\" +\n            \"<p>Implementing the <code>org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.Partitioner</code> interface allows you to plug in a custom partitioner.\";\n\n    /** <code>interceptor.classes</code> */\n    public static final String INTERCEPTOR_CLASSES_CONFIG = \"interceptor.classes\";\n    public static final String INTERCEPTOR_CLASSES_DOC = \"A list of classes to use as interceptors. \"\n                                                        + \"Implementing the <code>org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.ProducerInterceptor</code> interface allows you to intercept (and possibly mutate) the records \"\n                                                        + \"received by the producer before they are published to the Kafka cluster. this.originals().containsKey(CLIENT_ID_CONFIG);\n        if (userConfiguredClientId) {\n            refinedClientId = this.getString(CLIENT_ID_CONFIG);\n        } else {\n            String        }\n        configs.put(CLIENT_ID_CONFIG, refinedClientId);\n    }\n\n    private void postProcessAndValidateIdempotenceConfigs(final Map<String, Object> configs) {\n        final Map<String, Object> originalConfigs = this.originals();\n        final String acksStr = parseAcks(this.getString(ACKS_CONFIG));\n        configs.put(ACKS_CONFIG, acksStr);\n        final boolean userConfiguredIdempotence = this.originals().containsKey(ENABLE_IDEMPOTENCE_CONFIG);\n        boolean idempotenceEnabled = this.getBoolean(ENABLE_IDEMPOTENCE_CONFIG);\n        boolean shouldDisableIdempotence = false;\n\n        // For idempotence producers, values for `retries` and `acks` and `max.in.flight.requests.per.connection` need validation\n        if (idempotenceEnabled) {\n            final int retries = this.getInt(RETRIES_CONFIG);\n            if (retries == 0) {\n                if (userConfiguredIdempotence) {\n                    throw new ConfigException(\"Must set \" + RETRIES_CONFIG + \" to non-zero when using the idempotent producer.\");\n                }\n                log.info(\"Idempotence will be disabled because {} is set to 0.\", RETRIES_CONFIG);\n                shouldDisableIdempotence = true;\n            }\n\n            final short acks = Short.parseShort(acksStr);\n            if (acks != (short) -1) {\n                if (userConfiguredIdempotence) {\n                    throw new ConfigException(\"Must set \" + ACKS_CONFIG + \" to all in order to use the idempotent \" +\n                        \"producer. Otherwise we cannot guarantee idempotence.\");\n                }\n                log.info(\"Idempotence will be disabled because {} is set to {}, not set to 'all'.\", ACKS_CONFIG, acks);\n                shouldDisableIdempotence = true;\n            }\n\n            final int inFlightConnection = this.getInt(MAX_IN_FLIGHT_REQUESTS_PER_CONNECTION);\n            if (MAX_IN_FLIGHT_REQUESTS_PER_CONNECTION_FOR_IDEMPOTENCE < inFlightConnection) {\n                throw new ConfigException(\"To use the idempotent producer, \" + MAX_IN_FLIGHT_REQUESTS_PER_CONNECTION +\n                                          \" must be set to at most 5. Current value is \" + inFlightConnection + \".\");\n            }\n        }\n\n        if (shouldDisableIdempotence) {\n            configs.put(ENABLE_IDEMPOTENCE_CONFIG, false);\n            idempotenceEnabled = false;\n        }\n\n        // validate `transaction.id` after validating idempotence dependant configs because `enable.idempotence` config might be overridden\n        boolean userConfiguredTransactions = originalConfigs.containsKey(TRANSACTIONAL_ID_CONFIG);\n        if (!idempotenceEnabled && userConfiguredTransactions) {\n            throw new ConfigException(\"Cannot set a \" + ProducerConfig.TRANSACTIONAL_ID_CONFIG + \" without also enabling idempotence.\");\n        }\n\n        // Validate that transaction.timeout.ms is not set when transaction.two.phase.commit.enable is true\n        // In standard Kafka transactions, the broker enforces transaction.timeout.ms and aborts any\n        // transaction that isn't completed in time. With two-phase commit (2PC), an external coordinator\n        // decides when to finalize, so broker-side timeouts don't apply. Disallow using both.\n        boolean enable2PC = this.getBoolean(TRANSACTION_TWO_PHASE_COMMIT_ENABLE_CONFIG);\n        boolean userConfiguredTransactionTimeout = originalConfigs.containsKey(TRANSACTION_TIMEOUT_CONFIG);\n        if (enable2PC && userConfiguredTransactionTimeout) {\n            throw new ConfigException(\n                \"Cannot set \" + ProducerConfig.TRANSACTION_TIMEOUT_CONFIG +\n                \" when \" + ProducerConfig.TRANSACTION_TWO_PHASE_COMMIT_ENABLE_CONFIG +\n                \" is set to true. \"3.4\"</code>) and during the second you remove it. This is required to safely handle 3 changes. The first is introduction of the new cooperative rebalancing protocol of the embedded consumer. The second is a change in foreign-key join serialization format.\n    39→        Note that you will remain using the old eager rebalancing protocol if you skip or delay the second rolling bounce, but you can safely switch over to cooperative at any time once the entire group is on 2.4+ by removing the config value and bouncing. For more details please refer to\n    40→        <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/vAclBg\">KIP-429</a>. The third is a change in the serialization format for an internal repartition topic. For more details, please refer to <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/P5VbDg\">KIP-904</a>:\n    41→    </p>\n    42→    <ul>\n    43→        <li> prepare your application instances for a rolling bounce and make sure that config <code>upgrade.from</code> is set to the version from which it is being upgrade.</li>\n    44→        <li> bounce each instance of your application once </li>\n    45→        <li> prepare your newly deployed {{fullDotVersion}} application instances for a second round of rolling bounces; make sure to remove the value for config <code>upgrade.from</code> </li>\n    46→        <li> bounce each instance of your application once more to complete the upgrade </li>\n    47→    </ul>\n    48→    <p> As an alternative, an offline upgrade is also possible. Upgrading from any versions as old as 0.10.0.x to {{fullDotVersion}} in offline mode require the following steps: </p>\n    49→    <ul>\n    50→        <li> stop all old (e.g., 0.10.0.x) application instances </li>\n    51→        <li> update your code and swap old code and jar file with new code and new jar file </li>\n    52→        <li> restart all new ({{fullDotVersion}}) application instances </li>\n    53→    </ul>\n    54→    <p>\n    55→        Note: The cooperative rebalancing protocol has been the default since 2.4, but we have continued to support the\n    56→        eager rebalancing protocol to provide users an upgrade path. This support will be dropped in a future release,\n    57→        so any users still on the eager protocol should prepare to finish upgrading their applications to the cooperative protocol in version 3.1.\n    58→        This only affects users who are still on a version older than 2.4, and users who have upgraded already but have not yet\n    59→        removed the <code>upgrade.from</code> config that they set when upgrading from a version below 2.4.\n    60→        Users fitting into the latter case will simply need to unset this config when upgrading beyond 3.1,\n    61→        while users in the former case will need to follow a slightly different upgrade path if they attempt to upgrade from 2.3 or below to a version above 3.1.\n    62→        Those applications will need to go through a bridge release, by first upgrading to a version between 2.4 - 3.1 and setting the <code>upgrade.from</code> config,\n    63→        then removing that config and upgrading to the final version above 3.1. See <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-8575\">KAFKA-8575</a>\n    64→        for more details.\n    65→    </p>\n    66→\n    67→    <p>For a table that shows Streams API compatibility with Kafka broker versions, see <a href=\"#streams_api_broker_compat\">Broker Compatibility</a>.</p>\n    68→\n    69→    <h3 class=\"anchor-heading\"><a id=\"streams_notable_changes\" class=\"anchor-link\"></a><a href=\"#streams_notable_changes\">Notable compatibility changes in past releases</a></h3>\n    70→\n    71→    <p>\n    72→        Starting in version 4.0.0, Kafka Streams will only be compatible when running against brokers on version 2.1\n    73→        or higher. Additionally, exactly-once semantics (EOS) will require brokers to be at least version 2.5.\n    74→    </p>\n    75→\n    76→    <p>\n    77→        Downgrading from 3.5.x or newer version to 3.4.x or older version needs special attention:\n    78→        Since 3.5.0 release, Kafka Streams uses a new serialization format for repartition topics.\n    79→        This means that older versions of Kafka Streams would not be able to recognize the bytes written by newer versions,\n    80→        and hence it is harder to downgrade Kafka Streams with version 3.5.0 or newer to older versions in-flight. For\n    81→        more details, please refer to <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/P5VbDg\">KIP-904</a>.\n    82→\n    83→        For a downgrade, first switch the config from <code>\"upgrade.from\"</code> to the version you are downgrading to.\n    84→        This disables writing of the new serialization format in your application. It's important to wait in this state\n    85→        long enough to make sure that the application has finished processing any \"in-flight\" messages written\n    86→        into the repartition topics in the new serialization format. Afterwards, you can downgrade your application to a\n    87→        pre-3.5.x version.\n    88→    </p>\n    89→\n    90→    <p>\n    91→        Downgrading from 3.0.x or newer version to 2.8.x or older version needs special attention:\n    92→        Since 3.0.0 release, Kafka Streams uses a newer RocksDB version whose on-disk format changed.\n    93→        This means that old versioned RocksDB would not be able to recognize the bytes written by that newer versioned RocksDB,\n    94→        and hence it is harder to downgrade Kafka Streams with version 3.0.0 or newer to older versions in-flight.\n    95→        Users need to wipe out the local RocksDB state stores written by the new versioned Kafka Streams before swapping in the\n    96→        older versioned Kafka Streams bytecode, which would then restore the state stores with the old on-disk format from the\n    97→        changelogs.\n    98→    </p>\n    99→\n   100→    <p>\n   101→        Kafka Streams does not support running multiple instances of the same application as different processes on the same physical state directory. Starting in 2.8.0 (as well as 2.7.1 and 2.6.2),\n   102→        this restriction will be enforced. If you wish to run more than one instance of Kafka Streams, you must configure them with different values for <code>state.dir</code>.\n   103→    </p>\n   104→\n   105→    <p>\n   106→        Starting in Kafka Streams 2.6.x, a new processing mode is available, named EOS version 2. This can be configured\n   107→        by setting <code>\"processing.guarantee\"</code> to <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code> for\n   108→        application versions 3.0+, or setting it to <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> for versions between 2.6 and 2.8.\n   109→        To use this new feature, your brokers must be on version 2.5.x or newer.\n   110→        If you want to upgrade your EOS application from an older version and enable this feature in version 3.0+,\n   111→        you first need to upgrade your application to version 3.0.x, staying on <code>\"exactly_once\"</code>,\n   112→        and then do second round of rolling bounces to switch to <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code>. If you\n   113→        are upgrading an EOS application from an older (pre-2.6) version to a version between 2.6 and 2.8, follow these\n   114→        same steps but with the config <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> instead. No special steps are required\n   115→        to upgrade an application using <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> from version 2.6+ to 3.0 or higher: you can\n   116→        just change the config from <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> to <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code> during the rolling upgrade.\n   117→        For a downgrade, do the reverse: first switch the config from <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code> to\n   118→        <code>\"exactly_once\"</code> to disable the feature in your 2.6.x application.\n   119→        Afterward, you can downgrade your application to a pre-2.6.x version.\n   120→    </p>\n   121→\n   122→    <p>Since 2.6.0 release, Kafka Streams depends on a RocksDB version that requires MacOS 10.14 or higher.</p>\n   123→\n   124→    <p>\n   125→        To run a Kafka Streams application version 2.2.1, 2.3.0, or higher a broker version 0.11.0 or higher is required\n   126→        and the on-disk message format must be 0.11 or higher.\n   127→        Brokers must be on version 0.10.1 or higher to run a Kafka Streams application version 0.10.1 to 2.2.0.\n   128→        Additionally, on-disk message format must be 0.10 or higher to run a Kafka Streams application version 1.0 to 2.2.0.\n   129→        For Kafka Streams 0.10.0, broker version 0.10.0 or higher is required.\n   130→    </p>\n   131→\n   132→    <p>\n   133→        In deprecated <code>KStreamBuilder</code> class, when a <code>KTable</code> is created from a source topic via <code>KStreamBuilder.table()</code>, its materialized state store\n   134→        will reuse the source topic as its changelog topic for restoring, and will disable logging to avoid appending new updates to the source topic; in the <code>StreamsBuilder</code> class introduced in 1.0, this behavior was changed\n   135→        accidentally: we still reuse the source topic as the changelog topic for restoring, but will also create a separate changelog topic to append the update records from source topic to. In the 2.0 release, we have fixed this issue and now users\n   136→        can choose whether or not to reuse the source topic based on the <code>StreamsConfig#TOPOLOGY_OPTIMIZATION_CONFIG</code>: if you are upgrading from the old <code>KStreamBuilder</code> class and hence you need to change your code to use\n   137→        the new <code>StreamsBuilder</code>, you should set this config value to <code>StreamsConfig#OPTIMIZE</code> to continue reusing the source topic; if you are upgrading from 1.0 or 1.1 where you are already using <code>StreamsBuilder</code> and hence have already\n   138→        created a separate changelog topic, you should set this config value to <code>StreamsConfig#NO_OPTIMIZATION</code> when upgrading to {{fullDotVersion}} in order to use that changelog topic for restoring the state store.\n   139→        More details about the new config <code>StreamsConfig#TOPOLOGY_OPTIMIZATION_CONFIG</code> can be found in <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/V53LB\">KIP-295</a>.\n   140→    </p>\n   141→\n   142→    <h3><a id=\"streams_api_changes_410\" href=\"#streams_api_changes_410\">Streams API changes in 4.1.0</a></h3>\n   143→\n   144→    <h4>Early Access of the Streams Rebalance Protocol</h4>\n   145→\n   146→    <p>\n   147→        The Streams Rebalance Protocol is a broker-driven rebalancing system designed specifically for Kafka\n   148→        Streams applications. Following the pattern of KIP-848, which moved rebalance coordination of plain consumers\n   149→        from clients to brokers, KIP-1071 extends this model to Kafka Streams workloads. Instead of clients\n   150→        computing new assignments on the client during rebalance events involving all members of the group, assignments are\n   151→        computed continuously on the broker. Instead of using a consumer group, the streams application registers as a\n   152→        streams group with the broker, which manages and exposes all metadata required for coordination of the\n   153→        streams application instances.\n   154→    </p>\n   155→\n   156→    <p>\n   157→        This Early Access release covers a subset of the functionality detailed in\n   158→        <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA/KIP-1071%3A+Streams+Rebalance+Protocol\">KIP-1071</a>.\n   159→        Do not use the new protocol in production. The API is subject to change in future\n   160→        releases.\n   161→    </p>\n   162→\n   163→    <p><strong>What's Included in Early Access</strong></p>\n   164→\n   165→    <ul>\n   166→        <li><strong>Core Streams Group Rebalance Protocol:</strong> The <code>group.protocol=streams</code> configuration\n   167→            enables the dedicated streams rebalance protocol. This separates streams groups from consumer groups and\n   168→            provides a streams-specific group membership lifecycle and metadata management on the broker.</li>\n   169→        <li><strong>Sticky Task Assignor:</strong> A basic task assignment strategy that minimizes task movement\n   170→            during rebalances is included.</li>\n   171→        <li><strong>Interactive Query Support:</strong> IQ operations are compatible with the new streams protocol.</li>\n   172→        <li><strong>New Admin RPC:</strong> The <code>StreamsGroupDescribe</code> RPC provides streams-specific metadata\n   173→            separate from consumer group information, with corresponding access via the <code>Admin</code> client.</li>\n   174→        <li><strong>CLI Integration:</strong> You can list, describe, and delete streams groups via the <code>kafka-streams-groups.sh</code> script.</li>\n   175→    </ul>\n   176→\n   177→    <p><strong>What's Not Included in Early Access</strong></p>\n   178→\n   179→    <ul>\n   180→        <li><strong>Static Membership:</strong> Setting a client `instance.id` will be rejected.</li>\n   181→        <li><strong>Topology Updates:</strong> If a topology is changed significantly (e.g., by adding new source topics\n   182→            or changing the number of sub-topologies), a new streams group must be created.</li>\n   183→        <li><strong>High Availability Assignor:</strong> Only the sticky assignor is supported.</li>\n   184→        <li><strong>Regular Expressions:</strong> Pattern-based topic subscription is not supported.</li>\n   185→        <li><strong>Reset Operations:</strong> CLI offset reset operations are not supported.</li>\n   186→        <li><strong>Protocol Migration:</strong> Group migration is not available between the classic and new streams protocols.</li>\n   187→    </ul>\n   188→\n   189→    <p><strong>Why Use the Streams Rebalance Protocol?</strong></p>\n   190→\n   191→    <ul>\n   192→        <li>\n   193→            <strong>Broker-Driven Coordination:</strong>\n   194→            Centralizes task assignment logic on brokers instead of the client. This provides consistent,\n   195→            authoritative task assignment decisions from a single coordination point and reduces the potential for\n   196→            split-brain scenarios.\n   197→        </li>\n   198→        <li>\n   199→            <strong>Faster, More Stable Rebalances:</strong>\n   200→            Reduces rebalance duration and impact by removing the global synchronization point. This minimizes\n   201→            application downtime during membership changes or failures.\n   202→        </li>\n   203→        <li>\n   204→            <strong>Better Observability:</strong>\n   205→            Provides dedicated metrics and admin interfaces that separate streams from consumer groups, leading to\n   206→            clearer troubleshooting with broker-side observability.\n   207→        </li>\n   208→    </ul>\n   209→\n   210→    <p>\n   211→        Enabling the protocol requires the brokers and clients are running Apache Kafka 4.1. It should be enabled\n   212→        only on new clusters for testing purposes.\n   213→        Set <code>unstable.feature.versions.enable=true</code> for controllers and brokers, and\n   214→        set <code>unstable.api.versions.enable=true</code> on the brokers as well. In your Kafka Streams application\n   215→        configuration, set <code>group.protocol=streams</code>.\n   216→        After the new feature is configured, check\n   217→\t<code>kafka-features.sh --bootstrap-server localhost:9092 describe</code>\n   218→\tand `streams.version` should now have FinalizedVersionLevel 1.\n   219→    </p>\n   220→\n   221→    <p>\n   222→        Migration between the classic consumer group protocol and the Streams Rebalance Protocol is not supported in\n   223→        either direction. An application using this protocol must use a new <code>application.id</code> that has not\n   224→        been used by any application on the classic protocol. Furthermore, this ID must not be in use as a\n   225→        <code>group.id</code> by any consumer (\"classic\" or \"consumer\") nor share-group application.\n   226→        It is also possible to delete a previous consumer group using <code>kafka-consumer-groups.sh</code> before\n   227→        starting the application with the new protocol, which will however also delete all offsets for that group.\n   228→    </p>\n   229→\n   230→    <p>\n   231→        To operate the new streams groups, explore the options of <code>kafka-streams-groups.sh</code> to list,\n   232→        describe, and delete streams groups. In the new protocol, <code>session.timeout.ms</code>,\n   233→        <code>heartbeat.interval.ms</code> and <code>num.standby.replicas</code> are group-level configurations,\n   234→        which are ignored when they are set on the client side. To use eos-v2, brokers must be running version 2.5 or later.\n   260→        Additionally, all deprecated methods, classes, APIs, and config parameters up to and including AK 3.5 release have been removed.\n   261→        A few important ones are listed below. The full list can be found in <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-12822\">KAFKA-12822</a>.\n   262→        <ul>\n   263→            <li><a Java and Scala</a></li>\n   265→            <li>\n   266→                <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16339\">\"transformer\" methods and classes in both Java and Scala</a>\n   267→                <ul>\n   268→                    <li>migrating from <code>KStreams#transformValues()</code> to <code>KStreams.processValues()</code> might not be safe\n   269→                        due to <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-19668\">KAFKA-19668</a>.\n   270→                        Please refer to the <a 272→                </ul>\n   273→            </li>\n   274→            <li><a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-12824\">kstream.KStream#branch in both Java and Scala</a></li>\n This is required to safely handle 3 changes. The first is introduction of the new cooperative rebalancing protocol of the embedded consumer. The second is a change in foreign-key join serialization format.\n        Note that you will remain using the old eager rebalancing protocol if you skip or delay the second rolling bounce, but you can safely switch over to cooperative at any time once the entire group is on 2.4+ by removing the config value and bouncing. For more details please refer to\n        <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/vAclBg\">KIP-429</a>. The third is a change in the serialization format for an internal repartition topic. For more details, please refer to <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/P5VbDg\">KIP-904</a>:\n    </p>\n    <ul>\n        <li> prepare your application instances for a rolling bounce and make sure that config <code>upgrade.from</code> is set to the version from which it is being upgrade.</li>\n        <li> bounce each instance of your application once </li>\n        <li> prepare your newly deployed {{fullDotVersion}} application instances for a second round of rolling bounces; make sure to remove the value for config <code>upgrade.from</code> </li>\n        <li> bounce each instance of your application once more to complete the upgrade </li>\n    </ul>\n    <p> As an alternative, an offline upgrade is also possible. Upgrading from any versions as old as 0.10.0.x to {{fullDotVersion}} in offline mode require the following steps: </p>\n    <ul>\n        <li> stop all old (e.g., 0.10.0.x) application instances </li>\n        <li> update your code and swap old code and jar file with new code and new jar file </li>\n        <li> restart all new ({{fullDotVersion}}) application instances </li>\n    </ul>\n    <p>\n        Note: The cooperative rebalancing protocol has been the default since 2.4, but we have continued to support the\n        eager rebalancing protocol to provide users an upgrade path. This support will be dropped in a future release,\n        so any users still on the eager protocol should prepare to finish upgrading their applications to the cooperative protocol in version 3.1.\n        This only affects users who are still on a version older than 2.4, and users who have upgraded already but have not yet\n        removed the <code>upgrade.from</code> config that they set when upgrading from a version below 2.4.\n        Users fitting into the latter case will simply need to unset this config when upgrading beyond 3.1,\n        while users in the former case will need to follow a slightly different upgrade path if they attempt to upgrade from 2.3 or below to a version above 3.1.\n        Those applications will need to go through a bridge release, by first upgrading to a version between 2.4 - 3.1 and setting the <code>upgrade.from</code> config,\n        then removing that config and upgrading to the final version above 3.1. See <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-8575\">KAFKA-8575</a>\n        for more details.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>For a table that shows Streams API compatibility with Kafka broker versions, see <a href=\"#streams_api_broker_compat\">Broker Compatibility</a>.</p>\n\n    <h3 class=\"anchor-heading\"><a id=\"streams_notable_changes\" class=\"anchor-link\"></a><a href=\"#streams_notable_changes\">Notable compatibility changes in past releases</a></h3>\n\n    <p>\n        Starting in version 4.0.0, Kafka Streams will only be compatible when running against brokers on version 2.1\n        or higher. Additionally, exactly-once semantics (EOS) will require brokers to be at least version 2.5.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        Downgrading from 3.5.x or newer version to 3.4.x or older version needs special attention:\n        Since 3.5.0 release, Kafka Streams uses a new serialization format for repartition topics.\n        This means that older versions of Kafka Streams would not be able to recognize the bytes written by newer versions,\n        and hence it is harder to downgrade Kafka Streams with version 3.5.0 or newer to older versions in-flight. For\n        more details, please refer to <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/P5VbDg\">KIP-904</a>.\n\n        For a downgrade, first switch the config from <code>\"upgrade.from\"</code> to the version you are downgrading to.\n        This disables writing of the new serialization format in your application. It's important to wait in this state\n        long enough to make sure that the application has finished processing any \"in-flight\" messages written\n        into the repartition topics in the new serialization format. Afterwards, you can downgrade your application to a\n        pre-3.5.x version.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        Downgrading from 3.0.x or newer version to 2.8.x or older version needs special attention:\n        Since 3.0.0 release, Kafka Streams uses a newer RocksDB version whose on-disk format changed.\n        This means that old versioned RocksDB would not be able to recognize the bytes written by that newer versioned RocksDB,\n        and hence it is harder to downgrade Kafka Streams with version 3.0.0 or newer to older versions in-flight.\n        Users need to wipe out the local RocksDB state stores written by the new versioned Kafka Streams before swapping in the\n        older versioned Kafka Streams bytecode, which would then restore the state stores with the old on-disk format from the\n        changelogs.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        Kafka Streams does not support running multiple instances of the same application as different processes on the same physical state directory. Starting in 2.8.0 (as well as 2.7.1 and 2.6.2),\n        this restriction will be enforced. If you wish to run more than one instance of Kafka Streams, you must configure them with different values for <code>state.dir</code>.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        Starting in Kafka Streams 2.6.x, a new processing mode is available, named EOS version 2. This can be configured\n        by setting <code>\"processing.guarantee\"</code> to <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code> for\n        application versions 3.0+, or setting it to <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> for versions between 2.6 and 2.8.\n        To use this new feature, your brokers must be on version 2.5.x or newer.\n        If you want to upgrade your EOS application from an older version and enable this feature in version 3.0+,\n        you first need to upgrade your application to version 3.0.x, staying on <code>\"exactly_once\"</code>,\n        and then do second round of rolling bounces to switch to <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code>. If you\n        are upgrading an EOS application from an older (pre-2.6) version to a version between 2.6 and 2.8, follow these\n        same steps but with the config <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> instead. No special steps are required\n        to upgrade an application using <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> from version 2.6+ to 3.0 or higher: you can\n        just change the config from <code>\"exactly_once_beta\"</code> to <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code> during the rolling upgrade.\n        For a downgrade, do the reverse: first switch the config from <code>\"exactly_once_v2\"</code> to\n        <code>\"exactly_once\"</code> to disable the feature in your 2.6.x application.\n        Afterward, you can downgrade your application to a pre-2.6.x version.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>Since 2.6.0 release, Kafka Streams depends on a RocksDB version that requires MacOS 10.14 or higher.</p>\n\n    <p>\n        To run a Kafka Streams application version 2.2.1, 2.3.0, or higher a broker version 0.11.0 or higher is required\n        and the on-disk message format must be 0.11 or higher.\n        Brokers must be on version 0.10.1 or higher to run a Kafka Streams application version 0.10.1 to 2.2.0.\n        Additionally, on-disk message format must be 0.10 or higher to run a Kafka Streams application version 1.0 to 2.2.0.\n        For Kafka Streams 0.10.0, broker version 0.10.0 or higher is required.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        In deprecated <code>KStreamBuilder</code> class, when a <code>KTable</code> is created from a source topic via <code>KStreamBuilder.table()</code>, its materialized state store\n        will reuse the source topic as its changelog topic for restoring, and will disable logging to avoid appending new updates to the source topic; in the <code>StreamsBuilder</code> class introduced in 1.0, this behavior was changed\n        accidentally: we still reuse the source topic as the changelog topic for restoring, but will also create a separate changelog topic to append the update records from source topic to. In the 2.0 release, we have fixed this issue and now users\n        can choose whether or not to reuse the source topic based on the <code>StreamsConfig#TOPOLOGY_OPTIMIZATION_CONFIG</code>: if you are upgrading from the old <code>KStreamBuilder</code> class and hence you need to change your code to use\n        the new <code>StreamsBuilder</code>, you should set this config value to <code>StreamsConfig#OPTIMIZE</code> to continue reusing the source topic; if you are upgrading from 1.0 or 1.1 where you are already using <code>StreamsBuilder</code> and hence have already\n        created a separate changelog topic, you should set this config value to <code>StreamsConfig#NO_OPTIMIZATION</code> when upgrading to {{fullDotVersion}} in order to use that changelog topic for restoring the state store.\n        More details about the new config <code>StreamsConfig#TOPOLOGY_OPTIMIZATION_CONFIG</code> can be found in <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/V53LB\">KIP-295</a>.\n    </p>\n\n    <h3><a id=\"streams_api_changes_410\" href=\"#streams_api_changes_410\">Streams API changes in 4.1.0</a></h3>\n\n    <h4>Early Access of the Streams Rebalance Protocol</h4>\n\n    <p>\n        The Streams Rebalance Protocol is a broker-driven rebalancing system designed specifically for Kafka\n        Streams applications. Following the pattern of KIP-848, which moved rebalance coordination of plain consumers\n        from clients to brokers, KIP-1071 extends this model to Kafka Streams workloads. Instead of clients\n        computing new assignments on the client during rebalance events involving all members of the group, assignments are\n        computed continuously on the broker. Instead of using a consumer group, the streams application registers as a\n        streams group with the broker, which manages and exposes all metadata required for coordination of the\n        streams application instances.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        This Early Access release covers a subset of the functionality detailed in\n        <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA/KIP-1071%3A+Streams+Rebalance+Protocol\">KIP-1071</a>.\n        Do not use the new protocol in production. The API is subject to change in future\n        releases.\n    </p>\n\n    <p><strong>What's Included in Early Access</strong></p>\n\n    <ul>\n        <li><strong>Core Streams Group Rebalance Protocol:</strong> The <code>group.protocol=streams</code> configuration\n            enables the dedicated streams rebalance protocol. This separates streams groups from consumer groups and\n            provides a streams-specific group membership lifecycle and metadata management on the broker.</li>\n        <li><strong>Sticky Task Assignor:</strong> A basic task assignment strategy that minimizes task movement\n            during rebalances is included.</li>\n        <li><strong>Interactive Query Support:</strong> IQ operations are compatible with the new streams protocol.</li>\n        <li><strong>New Admin RPC:</strong> The <code>StreamsGroupDescribe</code> RPC provides streams-specific metadata\n            separate from consumer group information, with corresponding access via the <code>Admin</code> client.</li>\n        <li><strong>CLI Integration:</strong> You can list, describe, and delete streams groups via the <code>kafka-streams-groups.sh</code> script.</li>\n    </ul>\n\n    <p><strong>What's Not Included in Early Access</strong></p>\n\n    <ul>\n        <li><strong>Static Membership:</strong> Setting a client `instance.id` will be rejected.</li>\n        <li><strong>Topology Updates:</strong> If a topology is changed significantly (e.g., by adding new source topics\n            or changing the number of sub-topologies), a new streams group must be created.</li>\n        <li><strong>High Availability Assignor:</strong> Only the sticky assignor is supported.</li>\n        <li><strong>Regular Expressions:</strong> Pattern-based topic subscription is not supported.</li>\n        <li><strong>Reset Operations:</strong> CLI offset reset operations are not supported.</li>\n        <li><strong>Protocol Migration:</strong> Group migration is not available between the classic and new streams protocols.</li>\n    </ul>\n\n    <p><strong>Why Use the Streams Rebalance Protocol?</strong></p>\n\n    <ul>\n        <li>\n            <strong>Broker-Driven Coordination:</strong>\n            Centralizes task assignment logic on brokers instead of the client. This provides consistent,\n            authoritative task assignment decisions from a single coordination point and reduces the potential for\n            split-brain scenarios.\n        </li>\n        <li>\n            <strong>Faster, More Stable Rebalances:</strong>\n            Reduces rebalance duration and impact by removing the global synchronization point. This minimizes\n            application downtime during membership changes or failures.\n        </li>\n        <li>\n            <strong>Better Observability:</strong>\n            Provides dedicated metrics and admin interfaces that separate streams from consumer groups, leading to\n            clearer troubleshooting with broker-side observability.\n        </li>\n    </ul>\n\n    <p>\n        Enabling the protocol requires the brokers and clients are running Apache Kafka 4.1. It should be enabled\n        only on new clusters for testing purposes.\n        Set <code>unstable.feature.versions.enable=true</code> for controllers and brokers, and\n        set <code>unstable.api.versions.enable=true</code> on the brokers as well. In your Kafka Streams application\n        configuration, set <code>group.protocol=streams</code>.\n        After the new feature is configured, check\n\t<code>kafka-features.sh --bootstrap-server localhost:9092 describe</code>\n\tand `streams.version` should now have FinalizedVersionLevel 1.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        Migration between the classic consumer group protocol and the Streams Rebalance Protocol is not supported in\n        either direction. An application using this protocol must use a new <code>application.id</code> that has not\n        been used by any application on the classic protocol. Furthermore, this ID must not be in use as a\n        <code>group.id</code> by any consumer (\"classic\" or \"consumer\") nor share-group application.\n        It is also possible to delete a previous consumer group using <code>kafka-consumer-groups.sh</code> before\n        starting the application with the new protocol, which will however also delete all offsets for that group.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        To operate the new streams groups, explore the options of <code>kafka-streams-groups.sh</code> to list,\n        describe, and delete streams groups. In the new protocol, <code>session.timeout.ms</code>,\n        <code>heartbeat.interval.ms</code> and <code>num.standby.replicas</code> are group-level configurations,\n        which are ignored when they are set on the client side. Use the <code>kafka-configs.sh</code> tool to set\n        these configurations, for example:\n        <code>kafka-configs.sh --bootstrap-server localhost:9092 --alter --entity-type groups\n            --entity-name wordcount --add-config streams.num.standby.replicas=1</code>.\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        Please provide feedback on this feature via the\n        <a href=\"https://kafka.apache.org/contact\">Kafka mailing lists</a> or by filing\n        <a href=\"https://kafka.apache.org/contributing\">JIRA issues</a>.\n    </p>\n\n    <h4>Other changes</h4>\n\n    <p>\n        The introduction of <a href=\"https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/x/4Y_MEw\">KIP-1111</a>\n        enables you to enforce explicit naming for all internal resources of the topology, including internal topics (e.g., changelog and repartition topics) and their associated state stores.\n        This ensures that every internal resource is named before the Kafka Streams application is deployed, which is essential for upgrading your topology.\n        You can enable this feature via <code>StreamsConfig</code> using the <code>StreamsConfig#ENSURE_EXPLICIT_INTERNAL_RESOURCE_NAMING_CONFIG</code> parameter.\n        When set to <code>true</code>, the application will refuse to start if any internal resource has an auto-generated name.\n    </p>\n    \n    <h3><a id=\"streams_api_changes_400\" href=\"#streams_api_changes_400\">Streams API changes in 4.0.0</a></h3>\n\n    <p>\n        In this release, eos-v1 (Exactly Once Semantics version 1) is no longer supported. To use eos-v2, brokers must be running version 2.5 or later.\n        Additionally, all deprecated methods, classes, APIs, and config parameters up to and including AK 3.5 release have been removed.\n        A few important ones are listed below. The full list can be found in <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-12822\">KAFKA-12822</a>.\n        <ul>\n            <li><a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-12829\">Old processor APIs</a></li>\n            <li><a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-12823\">KStream#through() in both Java and Scala</a></li>\n            <li>\n                <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16339\">\"transformer\" methods and classes in both Java and Scala</a>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>migrating from <code>KStreams#transformValues()</code> to <code>KStreams.processValues()</code> might not be safe\n                        due to <a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-19668\">KAFKA-19668</a>.\n                        Please refer to the <a href=\"/{{version}}/documentation/streams/developer-guide/dsl-api.html#transformers-removal-and-migration-to-processors\">migration guide</a> for more details.\n                    </li>\n                </ul>\n            </li>\n            <li><a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-12824\">kstream.KStream#branch in both Java and Scala</a></li>\n            <li><a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16332\">builder methods for Time/Session/Join/SlidingWindows</a></li>\n            <li><a href=\"https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-12827\">KafkaStreams#setUncaughtExceptionHandler()</a></li>\n        </ul>\n    </p>\n\n    <p>\n        In this release the <code>ClientInstanceIds</code> instance stores the global consumer<code>Uuid</code> for the\n        <a
